	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Biodiversity</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Variety and variability of life forms</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fungi_of_Saskatchewan.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Fungi_of_Saskatchewan.JPG/220px-Fungi_of_Saskatchewan.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Fungi_of_Saskatchewan.JPG/330px-Fungi_of_Saskatchewan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Fungi_of_Saskatchewan.JPG/440px-Fungi_of_Saskatchewan.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fungi_of_Saskatchewan.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A sampling of <a href="/wiki/Fungi" class="mw-redirect" title="Fungi">fungi</a> collected during summer 2008 in Northern <a href="/wiki/Saskatchewan" title="Saskatchewan">Saskatchewan</a> mixed woods, near LaRonge is an example regarding the species diversity of fungi. In this photo, there are also leaf <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">lichens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moss" title="Moss">mosses</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><b>Biodiversity</b> is the variety and <a href="/wiki/Genetic_variability" title="Genetic variability">variability</a> of <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">life on Earth</a>. Biodiversity is typically a measure of variation at the <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystem</a> level.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Terrestrial biodiversity is usually greater near the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> which is the result of the warm <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> and high <a href="/wiki/Primary_productivity" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary productivity">primary productivity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Biodiversity is not distributed evenly on <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>, and is richest in the tropics. These tropical forest ecosystems cover less than 10 percent of earth's surface, and contain about 90 percent of the world's species.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marine_biology" title="Marine biology">Marine biodiversity</a> is usually highest along coasts in the Western <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">sea surface temperature</a> is highest, and in the mid-latitudinal band in all oceans. There are <a href="/wiki/Latitudinal_gradients_in_species_diversity" title="Latitudinal gradients in species diversity">latitudinal gradients in species diversity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Biodiversity generally tends to cluster in <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">hotspots</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and has been increasing through time,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> but will be likely to slow in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rapid <a href="/wiki/Environmental_change" title="Environmental change">environmental changes</a> typically cause <a href="/wiki/Mass_extinction" class="mw-redirect" title="Mass extinction">mass extinctions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CockellKoeberl2006_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CockellKoeberl2006-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> More than 99.9 percent of all species that ever lived on Earth, amounting to over five billion species,<sup id="cite_ref-Book-Biology_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Book-Biology-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> are estimated to be <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinct</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-StearnsStearns2000_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StearnsStearns2000-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT-20141108-MJN_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20141108-MJN-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Estimates on the number of Earth's current <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> range from 10 million to 14 million,<sup id="cite_ref-MillerSpoolman2012_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MillerSpoolman2012-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> of which about 1.2 million have been documented and over 86 percent have not yet been described.<sup id="cite_ref-PLoS-20110823_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PLoS-20110823-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> More recently, in May 2016, scientists reported that 1 trillion species are estimated to be on Earth currently with only one-thousandth of one percent described.<sup id="cite_ref-NSF-2016002_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSF-2016002-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The total amount of related <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> <a href="/wiki/Base_pair" title="Base pair">base pairs</a> on Earth is estimated at 5.0 x 10<sup>37</sup> and weighs 50 billion <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">tonnes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT-20150718-rn_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20150718-rn-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In comparison, the total <a href="/wiki/Biomass_(ecology)" title="Biomass (ecology)">mass</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Biosphere" title="Biosphere">biosphere</a> has been estimated to be as much as 4 <a href="/wiki/Tonnes#Derived_units" class="mw-redirect" title="Tonnes">TtC</a> (trillion tons of <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">carbon</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-AGCI-2015_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AGCI-2015-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In July 2016, scientists reported identifying a set of 355 <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">genes</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Last_Universal_Common_Ancestor" class="mw-redirect" title="Last Universal Common Ancestor">Last Universal Common Ancestor</a> (LUCA) of all <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">organisms</a> living on Earth.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT-20160725_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20160725-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Age_of_the_Earth" title="Age of the Earth">age of the Earth</a> is about 4.54 billion years.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS1997_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS1997-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The earliest undisputed evidence of <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">life on Earth</a> dates at least from 3.5 billion years ago,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RavenJohnson2002_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RavenJohnson2002-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> during the <a href="/wiki/Eoarchean" title="Eoarchean">Eoarchean</a> Era after a geological <a href="/wiki/Crust_(geology)" title="Crust (geology)">crust</a> started to solidify following the earlier molten <a href="/wiki/Hadean" title="Hadean">Hadean</a> Eon. There are <a href="/wiki/Microbial_mat" title="Microbial mat">microbial mat</a> <a href="/wiki/Fossils" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossils">fossils</a> found in 3.48 billion-year-old <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> discovered in <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AP-20131113_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP-20131113-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TG-20131113-JP_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TG-20131113-JP-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AST-20131108_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AST-20131108-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Other early physical evidence of a <a href="/wiki/Biogenic_substance" title="Biogenic substance">biogenic substance</a> is <a href="/wiki/Graphite" title="Graphite">graphite</a> in 3.7 billion-year-old <a href="/wiki/Metasediment" class="mw-redirect" title="Metasediment">meta-sedimentary rocks</a> discovered in <a href="/wiki/Western_Greenland" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Greenland">Western Greenland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NG-20131208_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NG-20131208-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> More recently, in 2015, "remains of <a href="/wiki/Biotic_material" title="Biotic material">biotic life</a>" were found in 4.1 billion-year-old rocks in Western Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-AP-20151019_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP-20151019-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> According to one of the researchers, "If life arose relatively quickly on Earth .. then it could be common in the <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">universe</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-AP-20151019_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP-20151019-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since <a href="/wiki/Abiogenesis" title="Abiogenesis">life began on Earth</a>, five major <a href="/wiki/Mass_extinctions" class="mw-redirect" title="Mass extinctions">mass extinctions</a> and several minor events have led to large and sudden drops in biodiversity. The <a href="/wiki/Phanerozoic" title="Phanerozoic">Phanerozoic</a> eon (the last 540&#160;million years) marked a rapid growth in biodiversity via the <a href="/wiki/Cambrian_explosion" title="Cambrian explosion">Cambrian explosion</a>—a period during which the majority of <a href="/wiki/Multicellular_organism" title="Multicellular organism">multicellular</a> <a href="/wiki/Phylum" title="Phylum">phyla</a> first appeared.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The next 400&#160;million years included repeated, massive <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_loss" title="Biodiversity loss">biodiversity losses</a> classified as <a href="/wiki/Mass_extinction" class="mw-redirect" title="Mass extinction">mass extinction</a> events. In the <a href="/wiki/Carboniferous" title="Carboniferous">Carboniferous</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carboniferous_rainforest_collapse" title="Carboniferous rainforest collapse">rainforest collapse</a> led to a great loss of <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">plant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">animal</a> life.<sup id="cite_ref-SahneyBentonFerry2010RainforestCollapse_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SahneyBentonFerry2010RainforestCollapse-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Permian%E2%80%93Triassic_extinction_event" title="Permian–Triassic extinction event">Permian–Triassic extinction event</a>, 251&#160;million years ago, was the worst; vertebrate recovery took 30&#160;million years.<sup id="cite_ref-SahneyBenton2008RecoveryFromProfoundExtinction_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SahneyBenton2008RecoveryFromProfoundExtinction-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The most recent, the <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous%E2%80%93Paleogene_extinction_event" title="Cretaceous–Paleogene extinction event">Cretaceous–Paleogene extinction event</a>, occurred 65&#160;million years ago and has often attracted more attention than others because it resulted in the extinction of the <span class="nowrap">non-avian</span> <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">dinosaurs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The period since the emergence of <a href="/wiki/Humans" class="mw-redirect" title="Humans">humans</a> has displayed an ongoing biodiversity reduction and an accompanying loss of <a href="/wiki/Genetic_diversity" title="Genetic diversity">genetic diversity</a>. Named the <a href="/wiki/Holocene_extinction" title="Holocene extinction">Holocene extinction</a>, the reduction is caused primarily by <a href="/wiki/Human_impact_on_the_environment" title="Human impact on the environment">human impacts</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/Habitat_(ecology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Habitat (ecology)">habitat</a> destruction.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Conversely, biodiversity positively impacts <a href="/wiki/Health" title="Health">human health</a> in a number of ways, although a few negative effects are studied.<sup id="cite_ref-SalaMeyerson2009_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalaMeyerson2009-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> designated 2011–2020 as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Decade_on_Biodiversity" title="United Nations Decade on Biodiversity">United Nations Decade on Biodiversity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> and 2021-2030 as the United Nations Decade on Ecosystem Restoration <sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> According to a 2019 <i><a href="/wiki/Global_Assessment_Report_on_Biodiversity_and_Ecosystem_Services" title="Global Assessment Report on Biodiversity and Ecosystem Services">Global Assessment Report on Biodiversity and Ecosystem Services</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/IPBES" class="mw-redirect" title="IPBES">IPBES</a>, 25% of plant and animal species are threatened with extinction as the result of human activity.<sup id="cite_ref-IPBES-20190506_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPBES-20190506-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT-20190506_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20190506-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</ul>
</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_terminology">History of terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History of terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>1916 - The term <i>biological diversity</i> was used first by J. Arthur Harris in "The Variable Desert," Scientific American, <a href="/wiki/JSTOR" title="JSTOR">JSTOR</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/stable/6182">6182</a>: "The bare statement that the region contains a flora rich in genera and species and of diverse geographic origin or affinity is entirely inadequate as a description of its real biological diversity."</li>
<li>1975 - The term <i>natural diversity</i> was introduced (by The Science Division of The Nature Conservancy in a 1975 study, "The Preservation of Natural Diversity.")<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li>1980 - <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Lovejoy" title="Thomas Lovejoy">Thomas Lovejoy</a> introduced the term <i>biological diversity</i> to the scientific community in a book.<sup id="cite_ref-ConsBiol80_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ConsBiol80-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> It rapidly became commonly used.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1985 - According to <a href="/wiki/Edward_O._Wilson" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward O. Wilson">Edward O. Wilson</a>, the contracted form <i>biodiversity</i> was coined by W. G. Rosen: "The National Forum on BioDiversity ... was conceived by Walter G.Rosen ... Dr. Rosen represented the NRC/NAS throughout the planning stages of the project. Furthermore, he introduced the term <i>biodiversity</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1985 - The term "biodiversity" appears in the article, "A New Plan to Conserve the Earth's Biota" by Laura Tangley.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1988 - The term biodiversity first appeared in a publication.<sup id="cite_ref-WilsonSciences1988_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WilsonSciences1988-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The present - the term has achieved widespread use.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Definitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prior_term">Prior term</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prior term">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>"Biodiversity" is most commonly used to replace the more clearly defined and long established terms, <a href="/wiki/Species_diversity" title="Species diversity">species diversity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Species_richness" title="Species richness">species richness</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternate_terms">Alternate terms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Alternate terms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Biologists most often define biodiversity as the "totality of <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">genes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecosystems" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecosystems">ecosystems</a> of a region".<sup id="cite_ref-Larsson2001_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Larsson2001-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Davis_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davis-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> An advantage of this definition is that it seems to describe most circumstances and presents a unified view of the traditional types of biological variety previously identified:
</p>
<ul><li>taxonomic diversity (usually measured at the species diversity level)</li>
<li>ecological diversity (often viewed from the perspective of <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem_diversity" title="Ecosystem diversity">ecosystem diversity</a>)</li>
<li>morphological diversity (which stems from <a href="/wiki/Genetic_diversity" title="Genetic diversity">genetic diversity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">molecular diversity</a><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Functional_group_(ecology)" title="Functional group (ecology)">functional diversity</a> (which is a measure of the number of functionally disparate species within a population (e.g. different feeding mechanism, different motility, predator vs prey, etc.)<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>) This multilevel construct is consistent with Datman and Lovejoy.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wilcox_1982">Wilcox 1982</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Wilcox 1982">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An explicit definition consistent with this interpretation was first given in a paper by Bruce A. Wilcox commissioned by the <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_the_Conservation_of_Nature_and_Natural_Resources" class="mw-redirect" title="International Union for the Conservation of Nature and Natural Resources">International Union for the Conservation of Nature and Natural Resources</a> (IUCN) for the 1982 World National Parks Conference. Wilcox's definition was "Biological diversity is the variety of life forms...at all levels of biological systems (i.e., molecular, organismic, population, species and ecosystem)...".<sup id="cite_ref-wilcox84_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wilcox84-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Genetic:_Wilcox_1984">Genetic: Wilcox 1984</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Genetic: Wilcox 1984">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Biodiversity can be defined genetically as the diversity of alleles, genes and <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">organisms</a>. They study processes such as <a href="/wiki/Mutation" title="Mutation">mutation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gene_transfer" class="mw-redirect" title="Gene transfer">gene transfer</a> that drive evolution.<sup id="cite_ref-wilcox84_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wilcox84-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Nations_1992">United Nations 1992</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: United Nations 1992">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 1992 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Earth_Summit" title="Earth Summit">Earth Summit</a> defined "biological diversity" as "the variability among living organisms from all sources, including, 'inter alia', <a href="/wiki/Terrestrial_ecoregion" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrestrial ecoregion">terrestrial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marine_(ocean)" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine (ocean)">marine</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Marine_biology" title="Marine biology">aquatic ecosystems</a> and the ecological complexes of which they are part: this includes diversity within species, between species and of ecosystems".<sup id="cite_ref-Hawksworth1996_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hawksworth1996-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> This definition is used in the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hawksworth1996_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hawksworth1996-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gaston_and_Spicer_2004">Gaston and Spicer 2004</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Gaston and Spicer 2004">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gaston &amp; Spicer's definition in their book "Biodiversity: an introduction" is "variation of life at all levels of biological organization".<sup id="cite_ref-GastonSpicer2004_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GastonSpicer2004-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution">Distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Distribution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG/220px-Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG/330px-Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG/440px-Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Swiss_National_Park_131.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Temperate_coniferous_forest" title="Temperate coniferous forest">conifer forest</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Alps" title="Swiss Alps">Swiss Alps</a> (<a href="/wiki/Swiss_National_Park" title="Swiss National Park">National Park</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>Biodiversity is not evenly distributed, rather it varies greatly across the globe as well as within regions. Among other factors, the diversity of all living things (<a href="/wiki/Biota_(ecology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Biota (ecology)">biota</a>) depends on <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">temperature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Precipitation" title="Precipitation">precipitation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Altitude" title="Altitude">altitude</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soil" title="Soil">soils</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">geography</a> and the presence of other species. The study of the spatial distribution of <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">organisms</a>, species and <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a>, is the science of <a href="/wiki/Biogeography" title="Biogeography">biogeography</a>.
</p><p>Diversity consistently measures higher in the <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">tropics</a> and in other localized regions such as the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Floristic_Region" title="Cape Floristic Region">Cape Floristic Region</a> and lower in polar regions generally. <a href="/wiki/Rain_forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Rain forests">Rain forests</a> that have had wet climates for a long time, such as <a href="/wiki/Yasuni_National_Park" title="Yasuni National Park">Yasuní National Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, have particularly high biodiversity.<sup id="cite_ref-dotearth_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dotearth-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-journal.pone.0008767_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journal.pone.0008767-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Terrestrial biodiversity is thought to be up to 25 times greater than ocean biodiversity.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> A new method used in 2011, put the total number of species on Earth at 8.7 million, of which 2.1 million were estimated to live in the ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-Moraplos_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moraplos-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> However, this estimate seems to under-represent the diversity of microorganisms.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latitudinal_gradients">Latitudinal gradients</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Latitudinal gradients">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Latitudinal_gradients_in_species_diversity" title="Latitudinal gradients in species diversity">Latitudinal gradients in species diversity</a></div>
<p>Generally, there is an increase in biodiversity from the <a href="/wiki/Geographical_pole" title="Geographical pole">poles</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">tropics</a>. Thus localities at lower <a href="/wiki/Latitudes" class="mw-redirect" title="Latitudes">latitudes</a> have more species than localities at higher latitudes. This is often referred to as the latitudinal gradient in species diversity. Several ecological factors may contribute to the gradient, but the ultimate factor behind many of them is the greater mean temperature at the equator compared to that of the poles.<sup id="cite_ref-MoraRobertson2003_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoraRobertson2003-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Even though terrestrial biodiversity declines from the equator to the poles,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> some studies claim that this characteristic is unverified in <a href="/wiki/Aquatic_ecosystems" class="mw-redirect" title="Aquatic ecosystems">aquatic ecosystems</a>, especially in <a href="/wiki/Marine_ecosystems" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine ecosystems">marine ecosystems</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The latitudinal distribution of parasites does not appear to follow this rule.<sup id="cite_ref-MorandKrasnov2010_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MorandKrasnov2010-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, an alternative hypothesis ("the <a href="/wiki/Fractal" title="Fractal">fractal</a> biodiversity") was proposed to explain the biodiversity latitudinal gradient.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> In this study, the <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> pool size and the fractal nature of ecosystems were combined to clarify some general patterns of this gradient. This hypothesis considers <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">temperature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moisture" title="Moisture">moisture</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Net_primary_production" class="mw-redirect" title="Net primary production">net primary production</a> (NPP) as the main variables of an ecosystem niche and as the axis of the ecological <a href="/wiki/Hypervolume" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypervolume">hypervolume</a>. In this way, it is possible to build fractal hypervolumes, whose <a href="/wiki/Fractal_dimension" title="Fractal dimension">fractal dimension</a> rises up to three moving towards the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hotspots">Hotspots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Hotspots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">biodiversity hotspot</a> is a region with a high level of <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> species that have experienced great <a href="/wiki/Habitat_destruction" title="Habitat destruction">habitat loss</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The term hotspot was introduced in 1988 by <a href="/wiki/Norman_Myers" title="Norman Myers">Norman Myers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McKee2004_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKee2004-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> While hotspots are spread all over the world, the majority are forest areas and most are located in the <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">tropics</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Forest" title="Atlantic Forest">Atlantic Forest</a> is considered one such hotspot, containing roughly 20,000 plant species, 1,350 vertebrates and millions of insects, about half of which occur nowhere else.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The island of <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> are also particularly notable. <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> is characterized by high biodiversity, with the highest rate of species by area unit worldwide and it has the largest number of endemics (species that are not found naturally anywhere else) of any country. About 10% of the species of the Earth can be found in Colombia, including over 1,900 species of bird, more than in Europe and North America combined, Colombia has 10% of the world's mammals species, 14% of the amphibian species and 18% of the bird species of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_dry_deciduous_forests" title="Madagascar dry deciduous forests">Madagascar dry deciduous forests</a> and lowland rainforests possess a high ratio of <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Since the island separated from mainland <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> 66 million years ago, many species and ecosystems have evolved independently.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>'s 17,000 islands cover 735,355 square miles (1,904,560&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) and contain 10% of the world's <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">flowering plants</a>, 12% of mammals and 17% of <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">reptiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">birds</a>—along with nearly 240 million people.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Many regions of high biodiversity and/or endemism arise from specialized <a href="/wiki/Habitat" title="Habitat">habitats</a> which require unusual adaptations, for example, <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">alpine</a> environments in high <a href="/wiki/Mountain" title="Mountain">mountains</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">Northern European</a> peat <a href="/wiki/Bog" title="Bog">bogs</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Accurately measuring differences in biodiversity can be difficult. <a href="/wiki/Selection_bias" title="Selection bias">Selection bias</a> amongst researchers may contribute to biased empirical research for modern estimates of biodiversity. In 1768, Rev. <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_White" title="Gilbert White">Gilbert White</a> succinctly observed of his <a href="/wiki/Selborne" title="Selborne">Selborne, Hampshire</a> <i>"all nature is so full, that that district produces the most variety which is the most examined."</i><sup id="cite_ref-White1887_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-White1887-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Evolution">Evolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Evolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">Evolution</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Phanerozoic_Biodiversity.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Phanerozoic_Biodiversity.png/300px-Phanerozoic_Biodiversity.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Phanerozoic_Biodiversity.png/450px-Phanerozoic_Biodiversity.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Phanerozoic_Biodiversity.png/600px-Phanerozoic_Biodiversity.png 2x" data-file-width="627" data-file-height="371" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Phanerozoic_Biodiversity.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Apparent marine fossil diversity during the Phanerozoic<sup id="cite_ref-Rosing2010_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rosing2010-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chronology">Chronology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Chronology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Biodiversity is the result of 3.5 billion years of <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">evolution</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Origin_of_life" class="mw-redirect" title="Origin of life">origin of life</a> has not been definitely established by science, however some evidence suggests that life may already have been well-established only a few hundred million years after the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_the_Earth" title="Age of the Earth">formation of the Earth</a>. Until approximately 600 million years ago, all life consisted of <a href="/wiki/Microorganism" title="Microorganism">microorganisms</a> – <a href="/wiki/Archaea" title="Archaea">archaea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Unicellular_organism" title="Unicellular organism">single-celled</a> <a href="/wiki/Protozoan" class="mw-redirect" title="Protozoan">protozoans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protist" title="Protist">protists</a>.
</p><p>The history of biodiversity during the <a href="/wiki/Phanerozoic" title="Phanerozoic">Phanerozoic</a> (the last 540 million years), starts with rapid growth during the <a href="/wiki/Cambrian_explosion" title="Cambrian explosion">Cambrian explosion</a>—a period during which nearly every <a href="/wiki/Phylum_(biology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Phylum (biology)">phylum</a> of <a href="/wiki/Multicellular_organism" title="Multicellular organism">multicellular organisms</a> first appeared. Over the next 400 million years or so, invertebrate diversity showed little overall trend and vertebrate diversity shows an overall exponential trend.<sup id="cite_ref-Sahney,_S._2010_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sahney,_S._2010-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> This dramatic rise in diversity was marked by periodic, massive losses of diversity classified as <a href="/wiki/Mass_extinction" class="mw-redirect" title="Mass extinction">mass extinction</a> events.<sup id="cite_ref-Sahney,_S._2010_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sahney,_S._2010-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> A significant loss occurred when rainforests collapsed in the carboniferous.<sup id="cite_ref-SahneyBentonFerry2010RainforestCollapse_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SahneyBentonFerry2010RainforestCollapse-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The worst was the <a href="/wiki/Permian-Triassic_extinction_event" class="mw-redirect" title="Permian-Triassic extinction event">Permian-Triassic extinction event</a>, 251 million years ago. Vertebrates took 30 million years to recover from this event.<sup id="cite_ref-SahneyBenton2008RecoveryFromProfoundExtinction_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SahneyBenton2008RecoveryFromProfoundExtinction-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Fossil_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil record">fossil record</a> suggests that the last few million years featured the greatest biodiversity in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Earth" title="History of Earth">history</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sahney,_S._2010_81-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sahney,_S._2010-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> However, not all scientists support this view, since there is uncertainty as to how strongly the fossil record is biased by the greater availability and preservation of recent <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geologic</a> sections. Some scientists believe that corrected for sampling artifacts, modern biodiversity may not be much different from biodiversity 300 million years ago.,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> whereas others consider the fossil record reasonably reflective of the diversification of life.<sup id="cite_ref-Sahney,_S._2010_81-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sahney,_S._2010-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Estimates of the present global macroscopic species diversity vary from 2 million to 100 million, with a best estimate of somewhere near 9 million,<sup id="cite_ref-Moraplos_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moraplos-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> the vast majority <a href="/wiki/Arthropod" title="Arthropod">arthropods</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heywood_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heywood-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Diversity appears to increase continually in the absence of natural selection.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diversification">Diversification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Diversification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The existence of a <i>global carrying capacity</i>, limiting the amount of life that can live at once, is debated, as is the question of whether such a limit would also cap the number of species. While records of life in the sea shows a <a href="/wiki/Logistic_function" title="Logistic function">logistic</a> pattern of growth, life on land (insects, plants and tetrapods) shows an <a href="/wiki/Exponential_growth" title="Exponential growth">exponential</a> rise in diversity. As one author states, "Tetrapods have not yet invaded 64 per cent of potentially habitable modes and it could be that without human influence the ecological and <a href="/wiki/Taxonomy_(biology)" title="Taxonomy (biology)">taxonomic</a> diversity of tetrapods would continue to increase in an exponential fashion until most or all of the available ecospace is filled."<sup id="cite_ref-Sahney,_S._2010_81-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sahney,_S._2010-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It also appears that the diversity continue to increase over time, especially after mass extinctions.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the other hand, changes through the <a href="/wiki/Phanerozoic" title="Phanerozoic">Phanerozoic</a> correlate much better with the <a href="/wiki/Hyperbolic_growth" title="Hyperbolic growth">hyperbolic</a> model (widely used in <a href="/wiki/Population_biology" title="Population biology">population biology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Demography" title="Demography">demography</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macrosociology" title="Macrosociology">macrosociology</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Fossil" title="Fossil">fossil</a> biodiversity) than with exponential and logistic models. The latter models imply that changes in diversity are guided by a first-order <a href="/wiki/Positive_feedback" title="Positive feedback">positive feedback</a> (more ancestors, more descendants) and/or a <a href="/wiki/Negative_feedback" title="Negative feedback">negative feedback</a> arising from resource limitation. Hyperbolic model implies a second-order positive feedback. The hyperbolic pattern of the <a href="/wiki/World_population" title="World population">world population</a> growth arises from a second-order positive feedback between the population size and the rate of technological growth.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid18677962_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid18677962-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The hyperbolic character of biodiversity growth can be similarly accounted for by a feedback between diversity and community structure complexity. The similarity between the curves of biodiversity and human population probably comes from the fact that both are derived from the interference of the hyperbolic trend with cyclical and <a href="/wiki/Stochastic" title="Stochastic">stochastic</a> dynamics.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid18677962_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid18677962-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Most biologists agree however that the period since human emergence is part of a new mass extinction, named the <a href="/wiki/Holocene_extinction_event" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocene extinction event">Holocene extinction event</a>, caused primarily by the impact humans are having on the environment.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> It has been argued that the present rate of extinction is sufficient to eliminate most species on the planet Earth within 100 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Wilson2002_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson2002-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, in his <i>Biodiversity-related Niches Differentiation Theory</i>, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Cazzolla_Gatti" title="Roberto Cazzolla Gatti">Roberto Cazzolla Gatti</a> proposed that species themselves are the architects of biodiversity, by proportionally increasing the number of potentially available niches in a given ecosystem.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> This study led to the idea that biodiversity is <a href="/wiki/Autocatalytic" class="mw-redirect" title="Autocatalytic">autocatalytic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystem</a> of interdependent <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> can be, therefore, considered as an <a href="/wiki/Emergent_properties" class="mw-redirect" title="Emergent properties">emergent</a> <a href="/wiki/Autocatalytic_set" title="Autocatalytic set">autocatalytic set</a> (a self-sustaining network of mutually "<a href="/wiki/Catalytic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catalytic">catalytic</a>" entities), where one (group of) species enables the existence of (i.e., creates niches for) other species. This view offers a possible answer to the fundamental question of why so many species can <a href="/wiki/Coexistence_theory" title="Coexistence theory">coexist</a> in the same ecosystem.
</p><p>New species are regularly discovered (on average between 5–10,000 new species each year, most of them <a href="/wiki/Insect" title="Insect">insects</a>) and many, though discovered, are not yet classified (estimates are that nearly 90% of all <a href="/wiki/Arthropod" title="Arthropod">arthropods</a> are not yet classified).<sup id="cite_ref-heywood_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heywood-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Most of the terrestrial diversity is found in <a href="/wiki/Tropical_forest" title="Tropical forest">tropical forests</a> and in general, land has more species than the ocean; some 8.7 million species may exists on Earth, of which some 2.1 million live in the ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-Moraplos_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moraplos-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecosystem_services">Ecosystem services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ecosystem services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Field_Hamois_Belgium_Luc_Viatour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Field_Hamois_Belgium_Luc_Viatour.jpg/220px-Field_Hamois_Belgium_Luc_Viatour.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Field_Hamois_Belgium_Luc_Viatour.jpg/330px-Field_Hamois_Belgium_Luc_Viatour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Field_Hamois_Belgium_Luc_Viatour.jpg/440px-Field_Hamois_Belgium_Luc_Viatour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2468" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Field_Hamois_Belgium_Luc_Viatour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Summer field in <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> (Hamois). The blue flowers are <i><a href="/wiki/Centaurea_cyanus" title="Centaurea cyanus">Centaurea cyanus</a></i> and the red are <i><a href="/wiki/Papaver_rhoeas" title="Papaver rhoeas">Papaver rhoeas</a></i>.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem_services" title="Ecosystem services">ecosystem services</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_balance_of_evidence">The balance of evidence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: The balance of evidence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>"Ecosystem services are the suite of benefits that ecosystems provide to humanity."<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The natural species, or biota, are the caretakers of all ecosystems. It is as if the natural world is an enormous bank account of capital assets capable of paying life sustaining dividends indefinitely, but only if the capital is maintained.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>These services come in three flavors:
</p>
<ol><li>Provisioning services which involve the production of renewable resources (e.g.: food, wood, fresh water)<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Regulating services which are those that lessen environmental change (e.g.: climate regulation, pest/disease control)<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Cultural services represent human value and enjoyment (e.g.: landscape aesthetics, cultural heritage, outdoor recreation and spiritual significance)<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>
<p>There have been many claims about biodiversity's effect on these ecosystem services, especially provisioning and regulating services. After an exhaustive survey through peer-reviewed literature to evaluate 36 different claims about biodiversity's effect on ecosystem services, 14 of those claims have been validated, 6 demonstrate mixed support or are unsupported, 3 are incorrect and 13 lack enough evidence to draw definitive conclusions.<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Services_enhanced">Services enhanced</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Services enhanced">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Provisioning_services">Provisioning services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Provisioning services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Greater species diversity
</p>
<ul><li>of plants increases fodder yield (synthesis of 271 experimental studies).<sup id="cite_ref-the-functional-role-of-producer-diversity_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the-functional-role-of-producer-diversity-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>of plants (i.e. diversity within a single species) increases overall <a href="/wiki/Crop_yield" title="Crop yield">crop yield</a> (synthesis of 575 experimental studies).<sup id="cite_ref-grain-yield-increase-in-cereal-variety-mixtures_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grain-yield-increase-in-cereal-variety-mixtures-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Although another review of 100 experimental studies reports mixed evidence.<sup id="cite_ref-does-plant-diversity-benefit-agroecosystems_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-does-plant-diversity-benefit-agroecosystems-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>of trees increases overall <a href="/wiki/Wood_production" title="Wood production">wood production</a> (Synthesis of 53 experimental studies).<sup id="cite_ref-tree-growth-in-monocultures-and-mixed_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tree-growth-in-monocultures-and-mixed-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> However, there is not enough data to draw a conclusion about the effect of tree trait diversity on wood production.<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Regulating_services">Regulating services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Regulating services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Greater species diversity
</p>
<ul><li>of fish increases the stability of <a href="/wiki/Fisheries" class="mw-redirect" title="Fisheries">fisheries</a> yield (Synthesis of 8 observational studies)<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>of natural pest enemies decreases herbivorous pest populations (Data from two separate reviews; Synthesis of 266 experimental and observational studies;<sup id="cite_ref-annual-review-ecology-evolution-systematics-vol-40_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annual-review-ecology-evolution-systematics-vol-40-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Synthesis of 18 observational studies.<sup id="cite_ref-functional-richness-and-ecosystem-services-bird-pred_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-functional-richness-and-ecosystem-services-bird-pred-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-birds-as-predators-in-trop-agroforestry_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-birds-as-predators-in-trop-agroforestry-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Although another review of 38 experimental studies found mixed support for this claim, suggesting that in cases where mutual intraguild predation occurs, a single predatory species is often more effective<sup id="cite_ref-influence-of-intraguild-predation_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-influence-of-intraguild-predation-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>of plants decreases disease prevalence on plants (Synthesis of 107 experimental studies)<sup id="cite_ref-plant-diversity-enhances-provision-of-ecosystem-services_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plant-diversity-enhances-provision-of-ecosystem-services-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>of plants increases resistance to <a href="/wiki/Plant_invasion" class="mw-redirect" title="Plant invasion">plant invasion</a> (Data from two separate reviews; Synthesis of 105 experimental studies;<sup id="cite_ref-plant-diversity-enhances-provision-of-ecosystem-services_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plant-diversity-enhances-provision-of-ecosystem-services-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Synthesis of 15 experimental studies<sup id="cite_ref-biotic-resistance-to-exotic-plant-invasions_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biotic-resistance-to-exotic-plant-invasions-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>)</li>
<li>of plants increases carbon sequestration, but note that this finding only relates to actual uptake of carbon dioxide and not long term storage, see below; Synthesis of 479 experimental studies)<sup id="cite_ref-the-functional-role-of-producer-diversity_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the-functional-role-of-producer-diversity-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>plants increases <a href="/wiki/Soil_nutrient" class="mw-redirect" title="Soil nutrient">soil nutrient</a> <a href="/wiki/Remineralization" class="mw-redirect" title="Remineralization">remineralization</a> (Synthesis of 103 experimental studies)<sup id="cite_ref-plant-diversity-enhances-provision-of-ecosystem-services_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plant-diversity-enhances-provision-of-ecosystem-services-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>of plants increases soil organic matter (Synthesis of 85 experimental studies)<sup id="cite_ref-plant-diversity-enhances-provision-of-ecosystem-services_103-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plant-diversity-enhances-provision-of-ecosystem-services-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Services_with_mixed_evidence">Services with mixed evidence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Services with mixed evidence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Provisioning_services_2">Provisioning services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Provisioning services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul><li>None to date</li></ul>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Regulating_services_2">Regulating services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Regulating services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul><li>Greater species diversity of plants may or may not decrease herbivorous pest populations. Data from two separate reviews suggest that greater diversity decreases pest populations (Synthesis of 40 observational studies;<sup id="cite_ref-organic-agriculture-promotes-evenness-and-natural-pest-control_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-organic-agriculture-promotes-evenness-and-natural-pest-control-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Synthesis of 100 experimental studies).<sup id="cite_ref-does-plant-diversity-benefit-agroecosystems_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-does-plant-diversity-benefit-agroecosystems-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> One review found mixed evidence (Synthesis of 287 experimental studies<sup id="cite_ref-vegetational-diversity-and-arthropod-population-response_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vegetational-diversity-and-arthropod-population-response-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>), while another found contrary evidence (Synthesis of 100 experimental studies<sup id="cite_ref-plant-diversity-enhances-provision-of-ecosystem-services_103-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plant-diversity-enhances-provision-of-ecosystem-services-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>)</li>
<li>Greater species diversity of animals may or may not decrease disease prevalence on those animals (Synthesis of 45 experimental and observational studies),<sup id="cite_ref-impacts-of-biodiversity-on-infectious-diseases_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-impacts-of-biodiversity-on-infectious-diseases-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> although a 2013 study offers more support showing that biodiversity may in fact enhance disease resistance within animal communities, at least in amphibian frog ponds.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Many more studies must be published in support of diversity to sway the balance of evidence will be such that we can draw a general rule on this service.</li>
<li>Greater species and trait diversity of plants may or may not increase long term carbon storage (Synthesis of 33 observational studies)<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Greater pollinator diversity may or may not increase pollination (Synthesis of 7 observational studies),<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> but a publication from March 2013 suggests that increased native pollinator diversity enhances pollen deposition (although not necessarily fruit set as the authors would have you believe, for details explore their lengthy supplementary material).<sup id="cite_ref-wild-pollinators-enhance-fruit-set-of-crops_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wild-pollinators-enhance-fruit-set-of-crops-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Services_hindered">Services hindered</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Services hindered">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Provisioning_services_3">Provisioning services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Provisioning services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul><li>Greater species diversity of plants reduces primary production (Synthesis of 7 experimental studies)<sup id="cite_ref-the-functional-role-of-producer-diversity_95-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the-functional-role-of-producer-diversity-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Regulating_services_3">Regulating services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Regulating services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul><li>greater genetic and species diversity of a number of organisms reduces freshwater purification (Synthesis of 8 experimental studies, although an attempt by the authors to investigate the effect of detritivore diversity on freshwater purification was unsuccessful due to a lack of available evidence (only 1 <a href="/wiki/Observational_study" title="Observational study">observational study</a> was found<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Provisioning_services_4">Provisioning services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Provisioning services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul><li>Effect of species diversity of plants on biofuel yield (In a survey of the literature, the investigators only found 3 studies)<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Effect of species diversity of fish on fishery yield (In a survey of the literature, the investigators only found 4 experimental studies and 1 observational study)<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Regulating_services_4">Regulating services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Regulating services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul><li>Effect of species diversity on the stability of <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuel</a> yield (In a survey of the literature, the investigators did not find any studies)<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Effect of species diversity of plants on the stability of fodder yield (In a survey of the literature, the investigators only found 2 studies)<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Effect of species diversity of plants on the stability of crop yield (In a survey of the literature, the investigators only found 1 study)<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Effect of <a href="/wiki/Genetic_diversity" title="Genetic diversity">genetic diversity</a> of plants on the stability of crop yield (In a survey of the literature, the investigators only found 2 studies)<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Effect of diversity on the stability of wood production (In a survey of the literature, the investigators could not find any studies)<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Effect of species diversity of multiple taxa on <a href="/wiki/Erosion_control" title="Erosion control">erosion control</a> (In a survey of the literature, the investigators could not find any studies – they did however find studies on the effect of species diversity and root biomass)<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Effect of diversity on <a href="/w/index.php?title=Flood_regulation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Flood regulation (page does not exist)">flood regulation</a> (In a survey of the literature, the investigators could not find any studies)<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Effect of species and trait diversity of plants on <a href="/wiki/Soil_moisture" class="mw-redirect" title="Soil moisture">soil moisture</a> (In a survey of the literature, the investigators only found 2 studies)<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Other sources have reported somewhat conflicting results and in 1997 Robert Costanza and his colleagues reported the estimated global value of ecosystem services (not captured in traditional markets) at an average of $33 trillion annually.<sup id="cite_ref-nature.com_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nature.com-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Stone_age" class="mw-redirect" title="Stone age">stone age</a>, species loss has accelerated above the average basal rate, driven by human activity. Estimates of species losses are at a rate 100-10,000 times as fast as is typical in the fossil record.<sup id="cite_ref-Hassan2005_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hassan2005-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
Biodiversity also affords many non-material benefits including spiritual and aesthetic values, knowledge systems and education.<sup id="cite_ref-Hassan2005_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hassan2005-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_biodiversity" title="Agricultural biodiversity">Agricultural biodiversity</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amazon_Manaus_forest.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Amazon_Manaus_forest.jpg/250px-Amazon_Manaus_forest.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Amazon_Manaus_forest.jpg/375px-Amazon_Manaus_forest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Amazon_Manaus_forest.jpg/500px-Amazon_Manaus_forest.jpg 2x" data-file-width="964" data-file-height="415" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amazon_Manaus_forest.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amazon_Rainforest" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Rainforest">Amazon Rainforest</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a></div></div></div>
<p>Agricultural diversity can be divided into two categories: <a href="/wiki/Genetic_diversity" title="Genetic diversity">intraspecific diversity</a>, which includes the genetic variety within a single species, like the potato (<i><a href="/wiki/Solanum_tuberosum" class="mw-redirect" title="Solanum tuberosum">Solanum tuberosum</a></i>) that is composed of many different forms and types (e.g. in the U.S. they might compare russet potatoes with new potatoes or purple potatoes, all different, but all part of the same species, <i>S. tuberosum</i>).
</p><p>The other category of agricultural diversity is called <a href="/wiki/Species_diversity" title="Species diversity">interspecific diversity</a> and refers to the number and types of different species. Thinking about this diversity we might note that many small vegetable farmers grow many different crops like potatoes and also carrots, peppers, lettuce etc.
</p><p>Agricultural diversity can also be divided by whether it is ‘planned’ diversity or ‘associated’ diversity. This is a functional classification that we impose and not an intrinsic feature of life or diversity. Planned diversity includes the crops which a farmer has encouraged, planted or raised (e.g. crops, covers, symbionts and livestock, among others), which can be contrasted with the associated diversity that arrives among the crops, uninvited (e.g. herbivores, weed species and pathogens, among others).<sup id="cite_ref-ecology-of-agroecosystems_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecology-of-agroecosystems-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The control of associated biodiversity is one of the great agricultural challenges that farmers face. On <a href="/wiki/Monoculture" title="Monoculture">monoculture</a> farms, the approach is generally to eradicate associated diversity using a suite of biologically destructive <a href="/wiki/Pesticide" title="Pesticide">pesticides</a>, mechanized tools and <a href="/wiki/Genetically_modified_organism" title="Genetically modified organism">transgenic engineering techniques</a>, then to <a href="/wiki/Crop_rotation" title="Crop rotation">rotate crops</a>. Although some <a href="/wiki/Polyculture" title="Polyculture">polyculture</a> farmers use the same techniques, they also employ <a href="/wiki/Integrated_pest_management" title="Integrated pest management">integrated pest management</a> strategies as well as strategies that are more labor-intensive, but generally less dependent on capital, biotechnology and energy.
</p><p>Interspecific crop diversity is, in part, responsible for offering variety in what we eat. Intraspecific diversity, the variety of alleles within a single species, also offers us choice in our diets. If a crop fails in a monoculture, we rely on agricultural diversity to replant the land with something new. If a wheat crop is destroyed by a pest we may plant a hardier variety of wheat the next year, relying on intraspecific diversity. We may forgo wheat production in that area and plant a different species altogether, relying on interspecific diversity. Even an agricultural society which primarily grows monocultures, relies on biodiversity at some point.
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_(Ireland)" title="Great Famine (Ireland)">Irish potato blight</a> of 1846 was a major factor in the deaths of one million people and the emigration of about two million. It was the result of planting only two potato varieties, both vulnerable to the blight, <i><a href="/wiki/Phytophthora_infestans" title="Phytophthora infestans">Phytophthora infestans</a></i>, which arrived in 1845<sup id="cite_ref-ecology-of-agroecosystems_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecology-of-agroecosystems-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>When <a href="/wiki/Rice_grassy_stunt_virus" title="Rice grassy stunt virus">rice grassy stunt virus</a> struck rice fields from Indonesia to India in the 1970s, 6,273 varieties were tested for resistance.<sup id="cite_ref-RGSV_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RGSV-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Only one was resistant, an Indian variety and known to science only since 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-RGSV_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RGSV-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> This variety formed a hybrid with other varieties and is now widely grown.<sup id="cite_ref-RGSV_113-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RGSV-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coffee_rust" class="mw-redirect" title="Coffee rust">Coffee rust</a> attacked coffee plantations in <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and Central America in 1970. A resistant variety was found in Ethiopia.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The diseases are themselves a form of biodiversity.</li></ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/Monoculture" title="Monoculture">Monoculture</a> was a contributing factor to several agricultural disasters, including the European wine industry collapse in the late 19th century and the US <a href="/wiki/Southern_corn_leaf_blight" title="Southern corn leaf blight">southern corn leaf blight</a> epidemic of 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although about 80 percent of humans' food supply comes from just 20 kinds of plants,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> humans use at least 40,000 species.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Many people depend on these species for food, shelter and clothing.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Earth's surviving biodiversity provides resources for increasing the range of food and other products suitable for human use, although the present extinction rate shrinks that potential.<sup id="cite_ref-Wilson2002_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson2002-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_health">Human health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Human health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
