<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Forest_fruits_from_Barro_Colorado.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Forest_fruits_from_Barro_Colorado.png/170px-Forest_fruits_from_Barro_Colorado.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Forest_fruits_from_Barro_Colorado.png/255px-Forest_fruits_from_Barro_Colorado.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Forest_fruits_from_Barro_Colorado.png/340px-Forest_fruits_from_Barro_Colorado.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1470" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Forest_fruits_from_Barro_Colorado.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The diverse forest canopy on <a href="/wiki/Barro_Colorado_Island" title="Barro Colorado Island">Barro Colorado Island</a>, Panama, yielded this display of different fruit</div></div></div>
<p>Biodiversity's relevance to human health is becoming an international political issue, as scientific evidence builds on the global health implications of biodiversity loss.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-biodiversity1_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biodiversity1-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
<sup id="cite_ref-CorvalánHales2005_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CorvalánHales2005-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> This issue is closely linked with the issue of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> as many of the anticipated <a href="/wiki/Health_risks_of_climate_change" class="mw-redirect" title="Health risks of climate change">health risks of climate change</a> are associated with changes in biodiversity (e.g. changes in populations and distribution of disease vectors, scarcity of fresh water, impacts on agricultural biodiversity and food resources etc.). This is because the species most likely to disappear are those that buffer against infectious disease transmission, while surviving species tend to be the ones that increase disease transmission, such as that of West Nile Virus, Lyme disease and Hantavirus, according to a study done co-authored by Felicia Keesing, an ecologist at Bard College and Drew Harvell, associate director for Environment of the <a href="/wiki/Atkinson_Center_for_a_Sustainable_Future" title="Atkinson Center for a Sustainable Future">Atkinson Center for a Sustainable Future</a> (ACSF) at <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The growing demand and lack of drinkable water on the planet presents an additional challenge to the future of human health. Partly, the problem lies in the success of water suppliers to increase supplies and failure of groups promoting preservation of water resources.<sup id="cite_ref-Bank2010_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bank2010-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> While the distribution of clean water increases, in some parts of the world it remains unequal. According to the World Health Organisation (2018) only 71% of the global population used a safely managed drinking-water service.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some of the health issues influenced by biodiversity include dietary health and nutrition security, infectious disease, medical science and medicinal resources, social and psychological health.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Biodiversity is also known to have an important role in reducing disaster risk and in post-disaster relief and recovery efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Biodiversity provides critical support for drug discovery and the availability of medicinal resources.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> A significant proportion of drugs are derived, directly or indirectly, from biological sources: at least 50% of the pharmaceutical compounds on the US market are derived from plants, animals and <a href="/wiki/Microorganism" title="Microorganism">microorganisms</a>, while about 80% of the world population depends on medicines from nature (used in either modern or traditional medical practice) for primary healthcare.<sup id="cite_ref-biodiversity1_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biodiversity1-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Only a tiny fraction of wild species has been investigated for medical potential. Biodiversity has been critical to advances throughout the field of <a href="/wiki/Bionics" title="Bionics">bionics</a>. Evidence from market analysis and biodiversity science indicates that the decline in output from the pharmaceutical sector since the mid-1980s can be attributed to a move away from natural product exploration ("bioprospecting") in favor of genomics and synthetic chemistry, indeed claims about the value of undiscovered pharmaceuticals may not provide enough incentive for companies in free markets to search for them because of the high cost of development;<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> meanwhile, natural products have a long history of supporting significant economic and health innovation.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Marine ecosystems are particularly important,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> although inappropriate <a href="/wiki/Bioprospecting" title="Bioprospecting">bioprospecting</a> can increase biodiversity loss, as well as violating the laws of the communities and states from which the resources are taken.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_and_industry">Business and industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Business and industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ueberladewagen_(jha).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg/220px-Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg/330px-Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg/440px-Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1094" data-file-height="710" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ueberladewagen_(jha).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a> production, pictured is a <a href="/wiki/Tractor" title="Tractor">tractor</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Chaser_bin" title="Chaser bin">chaser bin</a></div></div></div>
<p>Many industrial materials derive directly from biological sources. These include building materials, fibers, dyes, rubber and oil. Biodiversity is also important to the security of resources such as water, timber, paper, fiber and food.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> As a result, biodiversity loss is a significant risk factor in business development and a threat to long term economic sustainability.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Leisure.2C_cultural_and_aesthetic_value"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Leisure,_cultural_and_aesthetic_value">Leisure, cultural and aesthetic value</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Leisure, cultural and aesthetic value">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Biodiversity enriches leisure activities such as <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">hiking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birdwatching" title="Birdwatching">birdwatching</a> or natural history study. Biodiversity inspires <a href="/wiki/Musician" title="Musician">musicians</a>, painters, <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">sculptors</a>, writers and other artists. Many cultures view themselves as an integral part of the natural world which requires them to respect other living organisms.
</p><p>Popular activities such as <a href="/wiki/Gardening" title="Gardening">gardening</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fishkeeping" title="Fishkeeping">fishkeeping</a> and specimen collecting strongly depend on biodiversity. The number of species involved in such pursuits is in the tens of thousands, though the majority do not enter commerce.
</p><p>The relationships between the original natural areas of these often exotic animals and plants and commercial collectors, suppliers, breeders, propagators and those who promote their understanding and enjoyment are complex and poorly understood. The general public responds well to exposure to rare and unusual organisms, reflecting their inherent value.
</p><p>Philosophically it could be argued that biodiversity has intrinsic aesthetic and spiritual value to <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">mankind</a> <i>in and of itself</i>. This idea can be used as a counterweight to the notion that <a href="/wiki/Tropical_forest" title="Tropical forest">tropical forests</a> and other ecological realms are only worthy of conservation because of the services they provide.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecological_services">Ecological services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Ecological services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ecological_effects_of_biodiversity" title="Ecological effects of biodiversity">Ecological effects of biodiversity</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg/170px-Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg/255px-Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg/340px-Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="533" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Eagle_Creek_(Multnomah_County,_Oregon)" title="Eagle Creek (Multnomah County, Oregon)">Eagle Creek</a>, Oregon hiking</div></div></div>
<p>Biodiversity supports many <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem_services" title="Ecosystem services">ecosystem services</a>:
</p>
<blockquote><p>"There is now unequivocal evidence that biodiversity loss reduces the efficiency by which ecological communities capture biologically essential resources, produce biomass, decompose and recycle biologically essential nutrients... There is mounting evidence that biodiversity increases the stability of ecosystem functions through time... Diverse communities are more productive because they contain key species that have a large influence on productivity and differences in functional traits among organisms increase total resource capture... The impacts of diversity loss on ecological processes might be sufficiently large to rival the impacts of many other global drivers of environmental change... Maintaining multiple ecosystem processes at multiple places and times requires higher levels of biodiversity than does a single process at a single place and time."<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_92-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>It plays a part in regulating the chemistry of our <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere" title="Atmosphere">atmosphere</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">water supply</a>. Biodiversity is directly involved in <a href="/wiki/Water_purification" title="Water purification">water purification</a>, recycling <a href="/wiki/Nutrient" title="Nutrient">nutrients</a> and providing fertile soils. Experiments with controlled environments have shown that humans cannot easily build ecosystems to support human needs;<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> for example <a href="/wiki/Entomophily" title="Entomophily">insect pollination</a> cannot be mimicked, though there have been attempts to create artificial pollinators using <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicles" class="mw-redirect" title="Unmanned aerial vehicles">unmanned aerial vehicles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The economic activity of pollination alone represented between $2.1-14.6 billions in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Number_of_species">Number of species</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Number of species">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Global_biodiversity" title="Global biodiversity">Global biodiversity</a></div>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png/700px-Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png" decoding="async" width="700" height="334" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png/1050px-Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png/1400px-Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png 2x" data-file-width="4103" data-file-height="1958" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Discovered and predicted total number of species on land and in the oceans</div></div></div></div>
<p>According to Mora and colleagues, the total number of terrestrial species is estimated to be around 8.7 million while the number of oceanic species is much lower, estimated at 2.2 million. The authors note that these estimates are strongest for eukaryotic organisms and likely represent the lower bound of prokaryote diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-mora2011_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mora2011-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Other estimates include:
</p>
<ul><li>220,000 <a href="/wiki/Vascular_plants" class="mw-redirect" title="Vascular plants">vascular plants</a>, estimated using the species-area relation method<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>0.7-1 million marine species<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>10–30 million <a href="/wiki/Insect" title="Insect">insects</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> (of some 0.9 million we know today)<sup id="cite_ref-Le_Monde_newspaper_article_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Le_Monde_newspaper_article-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>5–10 million <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1.5-3 million <a href="/wiki/Fungi" class="mw-redirect" title="Fungi">fungi</a>, estimates based on data from the tropics, long-term non-tropical sites and molecular studies that have revealed <a href="/wiki/Cryptic_species" class="mw-redirect" title="Cryptic species">cryptic speciation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Some 0.075 million species of fungi had been documented by 2001)<sup id="cite_ref-Hawksworth_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hawksworth-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1 million <a href="/wiki/Mite" title="Mite">mites</a><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The number of <a href="/wiki/Microbial" class="mw-redirect" title="Microbial">microbial</a> species is not reliably known, but the <a href="/wiki/Global_Ocean_Sampling_Expedition" title="Global Ocean Sampling Expedition">Global Ocean Sampling Expedition</a> dramatically increased the estimates of genetic diversity by identifying an enormous number of new genes from near-surface <a href="/wiki/Plankton" title="Plankton">plankton</a> samples at various marine locations, initially over the 2004-2006 period.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> The findings may eventually cause a significant change in the way science defines <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> and other taxonomic categories.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Since the rate of extinction has increased, many extant species may become extinct before they are described.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Not surprisingly, in the <a href="/wiki/Animalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Animalia">animalia</a> the most studied groups are <a href="/wiki/Birds" class="mw-redirect" title="Birds">birds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mammals" class="mw-redirect" title="Mammals">mammals</a>, whereas <a href="/wiki/Fishes" class="mw-redirect" title="Fishes">fishes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arthropods" class="mw-redirect" title="Arthropods">arthropods</a> are the least studied <a href="/wiki/Animals" class="mw-redirect" title="Animals">animals</a> groups.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Measuring_biodiversity">Measuring biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Measuring biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Diversity_index" title="Diversity index">diversity index</a> and <a href="/wiki/Measurement_of_biodiversity" title="Measurement of biodiversity">measurement of biodiversity</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Species_loss_rates">Species loss rates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Species loss rates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Loss_of_biodiversity" class="mw-redirect" title="Loss of biodiversity">Loss of biodiversity</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>No longer do we have to justify the existence of humid tropical forests on the feeble grounds that they might carry plants with drugs that cure human disease. <a href="/wiki/Gaia_hypothesis" title="Gaia hypothesis"><i>Gaia theory</i></a> forces us to see that they offer much more than this. Through their capacity to evapotranspirate vast volumes of water vapor, they serve to keep the planet cool by wearing a sunshade of white reflecting cloud. Their replacement by cropland could precipitate a disaster that is global in scale.
</p></blockquote>
<p>During the last century, decreases in biodiversity have been increasingly observed. In 2007, German Federal Environment Minister <a href="/wiki/Sigmar_Gabriel" title="Sigmar Gabriel">Sigmar Gabriel</a> cited estimates that up to 30% of all species will be extinct by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Of these, about one eighth of known plant species are threatened with <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid_Reversing_loss_of_Biodiversity_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid_Reversing_loss_of_Biodiversity-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Estimates reach as high as 140,000 species per year (based on <a href="/wiki/Species-area_curve" class="mw-redirect" title="Species-area curve">Species-area theory</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> This figure indicates <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">unsustainable</a> ecological practices, because few species emerge each year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Almost all scientists acknowledge that the rate of species loss is greater now than at any time in human history, with extinctions occurring at rates hundreds of times higher than <a href="/wiki/Background_extinction" class="mw-redirect" title="Background extinction">background extinction</a> rates.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid_Reversing_loss_of_Biodiversity_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid_Reversing_loss_of_Biodiversity-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> As of 2012, some studies suggest that 25% of all mammal species could be extinct in 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In absolute terms, the planet has lost 58% of its biodiversity since 1970 according to a 2016 study by the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20180207105442/https://www.wnf.nl/custom/LPR_2016_fullreport/">World Wildlife Fund</a>. The Living Planet Report 2014 claims that "the number of mammals, birds, reptiles, amphibians and fish across the globe is, on average, about half the size it was 40 years ago". Of that number, 39% accounts for the terrestrial wildlife gone, 39% for the marine wildlife gone and 76% for the freshwater wildlife gone. Biodiversity took the biggest hit in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, plummeting 83 percent. High-income countries showed a 10% increase in biodiversity, which was canceled out by a loss in low-income countries. This is despite the fact that high-income countries use five times the ecological resources of low-income countries, which was explained as a result of process whereby wealthy nations are outsourcing <a href="/wiki/Resource_depletion" title="Resource depletion">resource depletion</a> to poorer nations, which are suffering the greatest ecosystem losses.<sup id="cite_ref-LivingPlanetReport2014_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LivingPlanetReport2014-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2017 study published in <i><a href="/wiki/PLOS_One" title="PLOS One">PLOS One</a></i> found that the biomass of insect life in Germany had declined by three-quarters in the last 25 years. Dave Goulson of <a href="/wiki/Sussex_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Sussex University">Sussex University</a> stated that their study suggested that humans "appear to be making vast tracts of land inhospitable to most forms of life, and are currently on course for ecological Armageddon. If we lose the insects then everything is going to collapse."<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Threats">Threats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Threats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2006, many species were formally classified as <a href="/wiki/Rare_species" title="Rare species">rare</a> or <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered</a> or <a href="/wiki/Threatened_species" title="Threatened species">threatened</a>; moreover, scientists have estimated that millions more species are at risk which have not been formally recognized. About 40 percent of the 40,177 species assessed using the <a href="/wiki/IUCN_Red_List" title="IUCN Red List">IUCN Red List</a> criteria are now listed as threatened with <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a>—a total of 16,119.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jared_Diamond" title="Jared Diamond">Jared Diamond</a> describes an "Evil Quartet" of <a href="/wiki/Habitat_destruction" title="Habitat destruction">habitat destruction</a>, overkill, introduced species and secondary extinctions.<sup id="cite_ref-MoultonSanderson1998_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoultonSanderson1998-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edward_O._Wilson" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward O. Wilson">Edward O. Wilson</a> prefers the <a href="/wiki/Acronym" title="Acronym">acronym</a> HIPPO, standing for <b>H</b>abitat destruction, <b>I</b>nvasive species, <b>P</b>ollution, human over-<b>P</b>opulation and <b>O</b>ver-harvesting.<sup id="cite_ref-Chen2003_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chen2003-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The most authoritative classification in use today is <a href="/wiki/IUCN" class="mw-redirect" title="IUCN">IUCN</a>'s Classification of Direct Threats<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> <small>(<i>version 2.0 released in 2016</i>)</small> which has been adopted by major international conservation organizations such as the US <a href="/wiki/Nature_Conservancy" class="mw-redirect" title="Nature Conservancy">Nature Conservancy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conservation_International" title="Conservation International">Conservation International</a> and <a href="/wiki/BirdLife_International" title="BirdLife International">BirdLife International</a>.
</p><p>The 11 main direct threats to conservation are:
</p><p><b>1.  residential &amp; commercial development</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>housing &amp; urban areas <i>(urban areas, suburbs, villages, vacation homes, shopping areas, offices, schools, hospitals)</i></li>
<li>commercial &amp; industrial areas <i>(manufacturing plants, shopping centers, office parks, military bases, power plants, train &amp; ship yards, airports)</i></li>
<li>tourism &amp; recreational areas <i>(skiing, golf courses, sports fields, parks, campgrounds)</i></li></ul></dd></dl>
<p><b>2.  farming activities</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>agriculture <i>(crop farms, orchards, vineyards, plantations, ranches)</i></li>
<li>aquaculture <i>(shrimp or fin fish aquaculture, fish ponds on farms, hatchery salmon, seeded shellfish beds, artificial algal beds)</i></li></ul></dd></dl>
<p><b>3.  energy production &amp; mining</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>renewable energy production <i>(geothermal, solar, wind, &amp; tidal farms)</i></li>
<li>non-renewable energy production <i>(oil and gas drilling)</i></li>
<li>mining <i>(fuel and minerals)</i></li></ul></dd></dl>
<p><b>4.  transportation &amp; service corridors</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>service corridors <i>(electrical &amp; phone wires, aqueducts, oil &amp; gas pipelines)</i></li>
<li>transport corridors <i>(roads, railroads, shipping lanes, and flight paths)</i></li>
<li>collisions with the vehicles using the corridors</li>
<li>associated accidents and catastrophes <i>(oil spills, electrocution, fire)</i></li></ul></dd></dl>
<p><b>5.  biological resource usages</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>hunting <i>(bushmeat, trophy, fur)</i></li>
<li>persecution <i>(predator control and pest control, superstitions)</i></li>
<li>plant destruction or removal <i>(human consumption, free range livestock foraging, battling timber disease, orchid collection)</i></li>
<li>logging or wood harvesting <i>(selective or clear cutting, firewood collection, charcoal production)</i></li>
<li>fishing <i>(trawling, whaling, live coral or seaweed or egg collection)</i></li></ul></dd></dl>
<p><b>6.  human intrusions &amp; activities that alter, destroy, simply disturb habitats and species from exhibiting natural behaviors</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>recreational activities <i>(off-road vehicles, motorboats, jet-skis, snowmobiles, ultralight planes, dive boats, whale watching, mountain bikes, hikers, birdwatchers, skiers, pets in recreational areas, temporary campsites, caving, rock-climbing)</i></li>
<li>war, civil unrest, &amp; military exercises <i>(armed conflict, mine fields, tanks &amp; other military vehicles, training exercises &amp; ranges, defoliation, munitions testing)</i></li>
<li>illegal activities <i>(smuggling, immigration, vandalism)</i></li></ul></dd></dl>
<p><b>7.  natural system modifications</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>fire suppression or creation <i>(controlled burns, inappropriate fire management, escaped agricultural and campfires, arson)</i></li>
<li>water management <i>(dam construction &amp; operation, wetland filling, surface water diversion, groundwater pumping)</i></li>
<li>other modifications <i>(reclamation projects, shoreline rip-rap, lawn cultivation, beach construction and maintenance, tree-thinning in parks)</i></li>
<li>removing/reducing human maintenance <i>(mowing meadows, reduction in controlled burns, lack of indigenous management of key ecosystems, ceasing supplemental feeding of condors)</i></li></ul></dd></dl>
<p><b>8.  invasive &amp; problematic species, pathogens &amp; genes</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>invasive species <i>(feral horses &amp; household pets, zebra mussels, Miconia tree, kudzu, introduction for biocontrol)</i></li>
<li>problematic native species <i>(overabundant native deer or kangaroo, overabundant algae due to loss of native grazing fish, locust-type plagues)</i></li>
<li>introduced genetic material <i>(pesticide-resistant crops, genetically modified insects for biocontrol, genetically modified trees or salmon, escaped hatchery salmon, restoration projects using non-local seed stock)</i></li>
<li>pathogens &amp; microbes <i>(plague affecting rodents or rabbits, Dutch elm disease or chestnut blight, Chytrid fungus affecting amphibians outside of Africa)</i></li></ul></dd></dl>
<p><b>9.  pollution</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>household sewage &amp; urban waste water <i>(discharge from municipal waste treatment plants, leaking septic systems, untreated sewage, outhouses, oil or sediment from roads, fertilizers and pesticides from lawns and golf-courses, road salt)</i></li>
<li>industrial &amp; military effluents <i>(toxic chemicals from factories, illegal dumping of chemicals, mine tailings, arsenic from gold mining, leakage from fuel tanks, PCBs in river sediments)</i></li>
<li>agricultural &amp; forestry effluents <i>(nutrient loading from fertilizer run-off, herbicide run-off, manure from feedlots, nutrients from aquaculture, soil erosion)</i></li>
<li>garbage &amp; solid waste <i>(municipal waste, litter &amp; dumped possessions, flotsam &amp; jetsam from recreational boats, waste that entangles wildlife, construction debris)</i></li>
<li>air-borne pollutants <i>(acid rain, smog from vehicle emissions, excess nitrogen deposition, radioactive fallout, wind dispersion of pollutants or sediments from farm fields, smoke from forest fires or wood stoves)</i></li>
<li>excess energy <i>(noise from highways or airplanes, sonar from submarines that disturbs whales, heated water from power plants, lamps attracting insects, beach lights disorienting turtles, atmospheric radiation from ozone holes)</i></li></ul></dd></dl>
<p><b>10. catastrophic geological events</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>earthquakes, tsunamis, avalanches, landslides, &amp; volcanic eruptions and gas emissions</li></ul></dd></dl>
<p><b>11. climate changes</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>ecosystem encroachment <i>(inundation of shoreline ecosystems &amp; drowning of coral reefs from sea level rise, sand dune encroachment from desertification)</i></li>
<li>changes in geochemical regimes <i>(ocean acidification, changes in atmospheric CO2 affecting plant growth, loss of sediment leading to broad-scale subsidence)</i></li>
<li>changes in temperature regimes <i>(heat waves, cold spells, oceanic temperature changes, melting of glaciers/sea ice)</i></li>
<li>changes in precipitation &amp; hydrological regimes <i>(droughts, rain timing, loss of snowcover, increased severity of floods)</i></li>
<li>severe weather events <i>(thunderstorms, tropical storms, hurricanes, cyclones, tornadoes, hailstorms, ice storms or blizzards, dust storms, erosion of beaches during storms)</i></li></ul></dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Habitat_destruction">Habitat destruction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Habitat destruction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amazonie_deforestation.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Amazonie_deforestation.jpg/220px-Amazonie_deforestation.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Amazonie_deforestation.jpg/330px-Amazonie_deforestation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Amazonie_deforestation.jpg/440px-Amazonie_deforestation.jpg 2x" data-file-width="778" data-file-height="618" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amazonie_deforestation.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">Deforestation</a> and increased road-building in the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Rainforest" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Rainforest">Amazon Rainforest</a> cause significant concern because of increased human encroachment upon wild areas, increased resource extraction and further threats to biodiversity.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Habitat_destruction" title="Habitat destruction">Habitat destruction</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Habitat_(ecology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Habitat (ecology)">Habitat</a> destruction has played a key role in extinctions, especially in relation to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_forest" title="Tropical forest">tropical forest</a> destruction.<sup id="cite_ref-EhrlichEhrlich1983_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EhrlichEhrlich1983-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Factors contributing to habitat loss include: <a href="/wiki/Overconsumption" title="Overconsumption">overconsumption</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_overpopulation" title="Human overpopulation">overpopulation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Land_use,_land-use_change_and_forestry" class="mw-redirect" title="Land use, land-use change and forestry">land use change</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a> (<a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">water pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soil_contamination" title="Soil contamination">soil contamination</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> or climate change.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Habitat size and numbers of species are systematically related. Physically larger species and those living at lower latitudes or in forests or oceans are more sensitive to reduction in habitat area.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Conversion to "trivial" standardized ecosystems (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Monoculture" title="Monoculture">monoculture</a> following <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>) effectively destroys habitat for the more diverse species that preceded the conversion. Even the simplest forms of agriculture affect diversity – through clearing/draining land, discouraging weeds and "pests", and encouraging just a limited set of domesticated plant and animal species. In some countries lack of property rights or lax law/regulatory enforcement necessarily leads to biodiversity loss (degradation costs having to be supported by the community).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>A 2007 study conducted by the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> found that biodiversity and genetic diversity are codependent—that diversity among species requires diversity within a species and <i>vice versa</i>. "If any one type is removed from the system, the cycle can break down and the community becomes dominated by a single species."<sup id="cite_ref-enn_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enn-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
At present<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the most threatened ecosystems occur in <a href="/wiki/Fresh_water" title="Fresh water">fresh water</a>, according to the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Ecosystem_Assessment" title="Millennium Ecosystem Assessment">Millennium Ecosystem Assessment</a> 2005, which was confirmed by the "Freshwater Animal Diversity Assessment" organised by the <a href="/wiki/GBIF" class="mw-redirect" title="GBIF">biodiversity platform</a> and the French <i><a href="/wiki/Institut_de_recherche_pour_le_d%C3%A9veloppement" title="Institut de recherche pour le développement">Institut de recherche pour le développement</a></i> (MNHNP).<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Co-extinctions are a form of <a href="/wiki/Habitat_destruction" title="Habitat destruction">habitat destruction</a>. Co-extinction occurs when the extinction or decline in one species accompanies similar processes in another, such as in plants and beetles.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2019 report has revealed that bees and other pollinating insects have been wiped out of almost a quarter of their habitats across the United Kingdom. The population crashes have been happening since 1980s and are affecting the biodiversity. The increase in industrial farming and pesticide use, combined with disease, invasive species and climate change is threatening the future of these insects and the agriculture they support.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Introduced_and_invasive_species">Introduced and invasive species</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Introduced and invasive species">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Introduced_species" title="Introduced species">Introduced species</a> and <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">Invasive species</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Male_Silver_Pheasant.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Male_Silver_Pheasant.jpg/220px-Male_Silver_Pheasant.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Male_Silver_Pheasant.jpg/330px-Male_Silver_Pheasant.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2b/Male_Silver_Pheasant.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Male_Silver_Pheasant.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Male <i>Lophura nycthemera</i> (<a href="/wiki/Silver_pheasant" title="Silver pheasant">silver pheasant</a>), a native of <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a> that has been introduced into parts of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> for ornamental reasons</div></div></div>
<p>Barriers such as large <a href="/wiki/River" title="River">rivers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea" title="Sea">seas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oceans" class="mw-redirect" title="Oceans">oceans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountains">mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deserts" class="mw-redirect" title="Deserts">deserts</a> encourage diversity by enabling independent evolution on either side of the barrier, via the process of <a href="/wiki/Allopatric_speciation" title="Allopatric speciation">allopatric speciation</a>. The term <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasive species</a> is applied to species that breach the natural barriers that would normally keep them constrained. Without barriers, such species occupy new territory, often supplanting native species by occupying their niches, or by using resources that would normally sustain native species.
</p><p>The number of species invasions has been on the rise at least since the beginning of the 1900s. Species are increasingly being moved by humans (on purpose and accidentally). In some cases the invaders are causing drastic changes and damage to their new habitats (e.g.: zebra mussels and the emerald ash borer in the Great Lakes region and the lion fish along the North American Atlantic coast). Some evidence suggests that invasive species are competitive in their new habitats because they are subject to less pathogen disturbance.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Others report confounding evidence that occasionally suggest that species-rich communities harbor many native and exotic species simultaneously<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> while some say that diverse ecosystems are more resilient and resist invasive plants and animals.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> An important question is, "do invasive species cause extinctions?" Many studies cite effects of invasive species on natives,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> but not extinctions. Invasive species seem to increase local (i.e.: <a href="/wiki/Alpha_diversity" title="Alpha diversity">alpha diversity</a>) diversity, which decreases turnover of diversity (i.e.: <a href="/wiki/Beta_diversity" title="Beta diversity">beta diversity</a>). Overall <a href="/wiki/Gamma_diversity" title="Gamma diversity">gamma diversity</a> may be lowered because species are going extinct because of other causes,<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> but even some of the most insidious invaders (e.g.: Dutch elm disease, emerald ash borer, chestnut blight in North America) have not caused their host species to become extinct. <a href="/wiki/Local_extinction" title="Local extinction">Extirpation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Population_decline" title="Population decline">population decline</a> and <a href="/wiki/Species_homogeneity" title="Species homogeneity">homogenization</a> of regional biodiversity are much more common. Human activities have frequently been the cause of invasive species circumventing their barriers,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> by introducing them for food and other purposes. Human activities therefore allow species to migrate to new areas (and thus become invasive) occurred on time scales much shorter than historically have been required for a species to extend its range.
</p><p>Not all introduced species are invasive, nor all invasive species deliberately introduced. In cases such as the <a href="/wiki/Zebra_mussel" title="Zebra mussel">zebra mussel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasion</a> of US waterways was unintentional. In other cases, such as <a href="/wiki/Mongoose" title="Mongoose">mongooses</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, the introduction is deliberate but ineffective (<a href="/wiki/Nocturnal" class="mw-redirect" title="Nocturnal">nocturnal</a> <a href="/wiki/Rat" title="Rat">rats</a> were not vulnerable to the <a href="/wiki/Diurnality" title="Diurnality">diurnal</a> mongoose). In other cases, such as <a href="/wiki/Oil_palm" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil palm">oil palms</a> in Indonesia and Malaysia, the introduction produces substantial economic benefits, but the benefits are accompanied by costly <a href="/wiki/Unintended_consequences" title="Unintended consequences">unintended consequences</a>.
</p><p>Finally, an introduced species may unintentionally injure a species that depends on the species it replaces. In <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prunus_spinosa" title="Prunus spinosa">Prunus spinosa</a> from Eastern Europe leafs much sooner than its West European counterparts, disrupting the feeding habits of the <i><a href="/wiki/Thecla_betulae" class="mw-redirect" title="Thecla betulae">Thecla betulae</a></i> butterfly (which feeds on the leaves). Introducing new species often leaves endemic and other local species unable to compete with the exotic species and unable to survive. The exotic organisms may be <a href="/wiki/Predator" class="mw-redirect" title="Predator">predators</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parasite" class="mw-redirect" title="Parasite">parasites</a>, or may simply outcompete indigenous species for nutrients, water and light.
</p><p>At present, several countries have already imported so many exotic species, particularly agricultural and ornamental plants, that their own indigenous fauna/flora may be outnumbered. For example, the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Kudzu" title="Kudzu">kudzu</a> from Southeast Asia to Canada and the United States has threatened biodiversity in certain areas.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Genetic_pollution">Genetic pollution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Genetic pollution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Genetic_pollution" title="Genetic pollution">Genetic pollution</a></div>
<p>Endemic species can be threatened with <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> through the process of <a href="/wiki/Genetic_pollution" title="Genetic pollution">genetic pollution</a>, i.e. uncontrolled <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_(biology)" title="Hybrid (biology)">hybridization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Introgression" title="Introgression">introgression</a> and genetic swamping. Genetic pollution leads to homogenization or replacement of local <a href="/wiki/Genomes" class="mw-redirect" title="Genomes">genomes</a> as a result of either a numerical and/or <a href="/wiki/Fitness_(biology)" title="Fitness (biology)">fitness</a> advantage of an introduced species.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
Hybridization and introgression are side-effects of introduction and invasion. These phenomena can be especially detrimental to <a href="/wiki/Rare_species" title="Rare species">rare species</a> that come into contact with more abundant ones. The abundant species can interbreed with the rare species, swamping its <a href="/wiki/Gene_pool" title="Gene pool">gene pool</a>. This problem is not always apparent from <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(biology)" title="Morphology (biology)">morphological</a> (outward appearance) observations alone. Some degree of <a href="/wiki/Gene_flow" title="Gene flow">gene flow</a> is normal adaptation and not all <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">gene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genotype" title="Genotype">genotype</a> constellations can be preserved. However, hybridization with or without introgression may, nevertheless, threaten a rare species' existence.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PottsBarbour2001_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PottsBarbour2001-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overexploitation">Overexploitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Overexploitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Overexploitation" title="Overexploitation">Overexploitation</a></div>
<p>Overexploitation occurs when a resource is consumed at an unsustainable rate. This occurs on land in the form of <a href="/wiki/Overhunting" class="mw-redirect" title="Overhunting">overhunting</a>, excessive <a href="/wiki/Logging" title="Logging">logging</a>, poor <a href="/wiki/Soil_conservation" title="Soil conservation">soil conservation</a> in agriculture and the illegal <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_trade" title="Wildlife trade">wildlife trade</a>.
</p><p>About 25% of world <a href="/wiki/Fishery" title="Fishery">fisheries</a> are now overfished to the point where their current biomass is less than the level that maximizes their sustainable yield.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Overkill_hypothesis" class="mw-redirect" title="Overkill hypothesis">overkill hypothesis</a>, a pattern of large animal extinctions connected with <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">human migration</a> patterns, can be used explain why <a href="/wiki/Megafauna" title="Megafauna">megafaunal</a> extinctions can occur within a relatively short time period.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Hybridization.2C_genetic_pollution.2Ferosion_and_food_security"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hybridization,_genetic_pollution/erosion_and_food_security">Hybridization, genetic pollution/erosion and food security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Hybridization, genetic pollution/erosion and food security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wheat_selection_k10183-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Wheat_selection_k10183-1.jpg/220px-Wheat_selection_k10183-1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/Wheat_selection_k10183-1.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="252" data-file-height="189" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wheat_selection_k10183-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Yecoro <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a> (right) <a href="/wiki/Cultivar" title="Cultivar">cultivar</a> is sensitive to salinity, plants resulting from a hybrid cross with cultivar W4910 (left) show greater tolerance to high salinity</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">Food security</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genetic_erosion" title="Genetic erosion">Genetic erosion</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">animal husbandry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Green_Revolution" title="Green Revolution">Green Revolution</a> popularized the use of conventional <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_(biology)" title="Hybrid (biology)">hybridization</a> to increase yield. Often hybridized breeds originated in developed countries and were further hybridized with local varieties in the developing world to create high yield strains resistant to local climate and diseases. Local governments and industry have been pushing hybridization. Formerly huge gene pools of various wild and indigenous breeds have collapsed causing widespread <a href="/wiki/Genetic_erosion" title="Genetic erosion">genetic erosion</a> and genetic pollution. This has resulted in loss of genetic diversity and biodiversity as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-bulletin28_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bulletin28-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Genetically_modified_organism" title="Genetically modified organism">Genetically modified organisms</a> contain genetic material that is altered through <a href="/wiki/Genetic_engineering" title="Genetic engineering">genetic engineering</a>. <a href="/wiki/Genetically_modified_crops" title="Genetically modified crops">Genetically modified crops</a> have become a common source for genetic pollution in not only wild varieties, but also in domesticated varieties derived from classical hybridization.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zaid1999_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaid1999-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Genetic erosion and genetic pollution have the potential to destroy unique <a href="/wiki/Genotype" title="Genotype">genotypes</a>, threatening future access to <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a>. A decrease in genetic diversity weakens the ability of crops and livestock to be hybridized to resist disease and survive changes in climate.<sup id="cite_ref-bulletin28_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bulletin28-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">Climate change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Climate change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effect_of_climate_change_on_plant_biodiversity" class="mw-redirect" title="Effect of climate change on plant biodiversity">Effect of climate change on plant biodiversity</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg/220px-Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg/330px-Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg/440px-Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1575" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Polar_bear" title="Polar bear">Polar bears</a> on the sea ice of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a>, near the <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">North Pole</a>. Climate change has started affecting bear populations.</div></div></div>
<p>Global warming is a major threat to global biodiversity.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kannan2009_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kannan2009-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> For example, coral reefs – which are biodiversity hotspots – will be lost within the century if global warming continues at the current rate.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Climate change has proven to affect biodiversity and evidence supporting the altering effects is widespread. Increasing atmospheric carbon dioxide certainly affects plant morphology<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> and is acidifying oceans,<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> and temperature affects species ranges,<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LovejoyHannah2005_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LovejoyHannah2005-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> phenology,<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> and weather,<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> but, mercifully, the major impacts that have been predicted are still potential futures. We have not documented major extinctions yet, even as climate change drastically alters the biology of many species.
</p><p>In 2004, an international collaborative study on four continents estimated that 10 percent of species would become extinct by 2050 because of global warming. "We need to limit climate change or we wind up with a lot of species in trouble, possibly extinct," said Dr. Lee Hannah, a co-author of the paper and chief climate change biologist at the Center for Applied Biodiversity Science at Conservation International.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A recent study predicts that up to 35% of the world terrestrial carnivores and ungulates will be at higher risk of extinction by 2050 because of the joint effects of predicted climate and land-use change under business-as-usual human development scenarios.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Climate change has advanced the time of evening when Brizillian free-tailed bats (Tadarida brasiliensis) emerge to feed.  This change is believed to be related to the drying of regions as temperatures rise. This earlier emergence exposes the bats to greater predation increased competition with other insectivores who feed in the twilight or daylight hours.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_overpopulation">Human overpopulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Human overpopulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_overpopulation" title="Human overpopulation">Human overpopulation</a></div>
<p>The world's population numbered nearly 7.6 billion as of mid-2017 (which is approximately one billion more inhabitants compared to 2005) and is forecast to reach 11.1 billion in 2100.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Sir <a href="/wiki/David_King_(scientist)" class="mw-redirect" title="David King (scientist)">David King</a>, former chief scientific adviser to the UK government, told a parliamentary inquiry: <i>"It is self-evident that the massive growth in the <a href="/wiki/Human_population" class="mw-redirect" title="Human population">human population</a> through the 20th century has had more impact on biodiversity than any other single factor."</i><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> At least until the middle of the 21st century, worldwide losses of pristine biodiverse land will probably depend much on the worldwide <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">human birth rate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> Biologists such as <a href="/wiki/Paul_R._Ehrlich" title="Paul R. Ehrlich">Paul R. Ehrlich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Pimm" title="Stuart Pimm">Stuart Pimm</a> have noted that <a href="/wiki/Human_population_growth" class="mw-redirect" title="Human population growth">human population growth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Overconsumption" title="Overconsumption">overconsumption</a> are the main drivers of species extinction.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to a 2014 study by the <a href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a>, the global human population already exceeds planet's <a href="/wiki/Biocapacity" title="Biocapacity">biocapacity</a> – it would take the equivalent of 1.5 Earths of biocapacity to meet our current demands.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> The report further points that if everyone on the planet had the Footprint of the average resident of Qatar, we would need 4.8 Earths and if we lived the lifestyle of a typical resident of the US, we would need 3.9 Earths.<sup id="cite_ref-LivingPlanetReport2014_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LivingPlanetReport2014-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Holocene_extinction">The Holocene extinction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: The Holocene extinction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Holocene_extinction" title="Holocene extinction">Holocene extinction</a></div>
<p>Rates of decline in biodiversity in this sixth mass extinction match or exceed rates of loss in the five previous <a href="/wiki/Extinction_event" title="Extinction event">mass extinction events</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Fossil_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil record">fossil record</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-proceedings1_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-proceedings1-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> Loss of biodiversity results in the loss of <a href="/wiki/Natural_capital" title="Natural capital">natural capital</a> that supplies <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem_services" title="Ecosystem services">ecosystem goods and services</a>. From the perspective of the method known as Natural Economy the economic value of 17 ecosystem services for Earth's <a href="/wiki/Biosphere" title="Biosphere">biosphere</a> (calculated in 1997) has an estimated value of US$33 trillion (3.3x10<sup>13</sup>) per year.<sup id="cite_ref-Costanza97_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Costanza97-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<pre>In 2019, a summary for policymakers of the largest, most comprehensive study to date of biodiversity and ecosystem services was published by the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Science-Policy_Platform_on_Biodiversity_and_Ecosystem_Services" title="Intergovernmental Science-Policy Platform on Biodiversity and Ecosystem Services">Intergovernmental Science-Policy Platform on Biodiversity and Ecosystem Services</a>. The report was finalised in Paris. The main conclusions:
</pre>
<p>1. Over the last 50 years, the state of nature has deteriorated at an unprecedented and accelerating rate.
</p><p>2. The main drivers of this deterioration have been changes in land and sea use, exploitation of living beings, climate change, pollution and invasive species. These five drivers, in turn, are caused by societal behaviors, from consumption to governance.
</p><p>3. Damage to ecosystems undermines 35 of 44 selected UN targets, including the UN General Assembly's  <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a> for poverty, hunger, health, water, cities' climate, oceans and land. It can cause problems with food, water and humanity's air supply.
</p><p>4. To fix the problem, humanity will need a transformative change, including <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_agriculture" title="Sustainable agriculture">sustainable agriculture</a>, reductions in <a href="/wiki/Consumption_(economics)" title="Consumption (economics)">consumption</a> and waste, fishing quotas and collaborative water management. In page 8 the report propose in page 8 of the summary " enabling visions of a good quality of life that do not entail ever-increasing material consumption" as one of the main measures. The report states that  "Some pathways chosen to achieve the goals related to energy, economic growth, industry and infrastructure and sustainable consumption and production (Sustainable Development Goals 7, 8, 9 and 12), as well as targets related to poverty, food security and cities (Sustainable Development Goals 1, 2 and 11), could have substantial positive or negative impacts on nature and therefore on the achievement of other Sustainable Development Goals"<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation">Conservation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Conservation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">Conservation biology</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MEAConservationStrategies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/MEAConservationStrategies.jpg/220px-MEAConservationStrategies.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/MEAConservationStrategies.jpg/330px-MEAConservationStrategies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/MEAConservationStrategies.jpg/440px-MEAConservationStrategies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1398" data-file-height="1398" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MEAConservationStrategies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A schematic image illustrating the relationship between biodiversity, ecosystem services, human well-being and poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> The illustration shows where conservation action, strategies and plans can influence the drivers of the current biodiversity crisis at local, regional, to global scales.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gletscherschmelze.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Gletscherschmelze.jpg/300px-Gletscherschmelze.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Gletscherschmelze.jpg/450px-Gletscherschmelze.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Gletscherschmelze.jpg/600px-Gletscherschmelze.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="519" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gletscherschmelze.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Retreat_of_glaciers_since_1850" title="Retreat of glaciers since 1850">retreat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Aletsch_Glacier" title="Aletsch Glacier">Aletsch Glacier</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Alps" title="Swiss Alps">Swiss Alps</a> (situation in 1979, 1991 and 2002), due to <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">Conservation biology</a> matured in the mid-20th century as <a href="/wiki/Ecologists" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecologists">ecologists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naturalists" class="mw-redirect" title="Naturalists">naturalists</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Scientists" class="mw-redirect" title="Scientists">scientists</a> began to research and address issues pertaining to global biodiversity declines.<sup id="cite_ref-Soule86_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soule86-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Davis96_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davis96-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dyke2008_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dyke2008-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The conservation ethic advocates management of <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a> for the purpose of sustaining biodiversity in <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecosystems" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecosystems">ecosystems</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">evolutionary process</a> and human culture and society.<sup id="cite_ref-proceedings1_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-proceedings1-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Soule86_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soule86-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dyke2008_232-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dyke2008-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hunter1996_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hunter1996-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Conservation biology is reforming around strategic plans to protect biodiversity.<sup id="cite_ref-Soule86_230-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soule86-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Soulé1986_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soulé1986-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> Preserving global biodiversity is a priority in strategic conservation plans that are designed to engage public policy and concerns affecting local, regional and global scales of communities, ecosystems and cultures.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> Action plans identify <a href="/wiki/Ecological_economics#Methodology" title="Ecological economics">ways</a> of sustaining human well-being, employing <a href="/wiki/Natural_capital" title="Natural capital">natural capital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capital_market" title="Capital market">market capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem_services" title="Ecosystem services">ecosystem services</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/w/index.php?title=EU_Directive_1999/22/EC&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="EU Directive 1999/22/EC (page does not exist)">EU Directive 1999/22/EC</a> zoos are described as having a role in the preservation of the biodiversity of wildlife animals by conducting research or participation in <a href="/wiki/Breeding_program" title="Breeding program">breeding programs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Protection_and_restoration_techniques">Protection and restoration techniques</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Protection and restoration techniques">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Removal of exotic species will allow the species that they have negatively impacted to recover their ecological niches. Exotic species that have become pests can be identified taxonomically (e.g.,&#160;with <a href="/wiki/Digital_Automated_Identification_SYstem" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital Automated Identification SYstem">Digital Automated Identification SYstem</a> (DAISY), using the <a href="/wiki/Consortium_for_the_Barcode_of_Life" title="Consortium for the Barcode of Life">barcode of life</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> Removal is practical only given large groups of individuals due to the economic cost.
</p><p>As sustainable populations of the remaining native species in an area become assured, "missing" species that are candidates for reintroduction can be identified using databases such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclopedia_of_Life#Resources_and_collaborations" title="Encyclopedia of Life">Encyclopedia of Life</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Global_Biodiversity_Information_Facility" title="Global Biodiversity Information Facility">Global Biodiversity Information Facility</a>.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_banking" title="Biodiversity banking">Biodiversity banking</a> places a monetary value on biodiversity. One example is the Australian <a href="/wiki/Native_Vegetation_Management_Framework" title="Native Vegetation Management Framework">Native Vegetation Management Framework</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gene_bank" title="Gene bank">Gene banks</a> are collections of specimens and genetic material. Some banks intend to reintroduce banked species to the ecosystem (e.g.,&#160;via tree nurseries).<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Reduction and better targeting of pesticides allows more species to survive in agricultural and urbanized areas.</li>
<li>Location-specific approaches may be less useful for protecting migratory species. One approach is to create <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_corridor" title="Wildlife corridor">wildlife corridors</a> that correspond to the animals' movements. National and other boundaries can complicate corridor creation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li></ul>
