<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Protected_areas">Protected areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Protected areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Protected areas are meant for affording protection to wild animals and their habitat which also includes forest reserves and biosphere reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> Protected areas have been set up all over the world with the specific aim of protecting and conserving plants and animals. Some scientists have called on the global community to designate as protected areas of 30 percent of the planet by 2030, and 50 percent by 2050, in order to mitigate biodiversity loss from anthropogenic causes.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_parks">National parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: National parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">National park</a></div>
<p>National park and nature reserve is the area selected by governments or private organizations for special protection against damage or degradation with the objective of biodiversity and landscape conservation. National parks are usually owned and managed by national or state governments. A limit is placed on the number of visitors permitted to enter certain fragile areas. Designated trails or roads are created. The visitors are allowed to enter only for study, cultural and recreation purposes. Forestry operations, grazing of animals and hunting of animals are regulated. Exploitation of habitat or wildlife is banned.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife_sanctuary">Wildlife sanctuary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Wildlife sanctuary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wildlife_sanctuary" class="mw-redirect" title="Wildlife sanctuary">Wildlife sanctuaries</a> aim only at conservation of species and have the following features:
</p>
<ol><li>The boundaries of the sanctuaries are not limited by state legislation.</li>
<li>The killing, hunting or capturing of any species is prohibited except by or under the control of the highest authority in the department which is responsible for the management of the sanctuary.</li>
<li>Private ownership may be allowed.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">Forestry</a> and other usages can also be permitted.</li></ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forest_reserves">Forest reserves</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Forest reserves">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">forests</a> play a vital role in harbouring more than 45,000 floral and 81,000 faunal species of which 5150 floral and 1837 faunal species are endemic.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Plant and animal species confined to a specific geographical area are called endemic species. In reserved forests, rights to activities like hunting and grazing are sometimes given to communities living on the fringes of the forest, who sustain their livelihood partially or wholly from forest resources or products. The unclassed forests covers 6.4 percent of the total forest area and they are marked by the following characteristics:
</p>
<ol><li>They are large inaccessible forests.</li>
<li>Many of these are unoccupied.</li>
<li>They are ecologically and economically less important.</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Steps_to_conserve_the_forest_cover">Steps to conserve the forest cover</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Steps to conserve the forest cover">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Forest_cover" title="Forest cover">forest cover</a></div>
<ol><li>An extensive <a href="/wiki/Reforestation" title="Reforestation">reforestation</a>/<a href="/wiki/Afforestation" title="Afforestation">afforestation</a> programme should be followed.</li>
<li>Alternative <a href="/wiki/Environment-friendly" class="mw-redirect" title="Environment-friendly">environment-friendly</a> sources of fuel energy such as <a href="/wiki/Biogas" title="Biogas">biogas</a> other than wood should be used.</li>
<li>Loss of biodiversity due to <a href="/wiki/Forest_fire" class="mw-redirect" title="Forest fire">forest fire</a> is a major problem, immediate steps to prevent forest fire need to be taken.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Overgrazing" title="Overgrazing">Overgrazing</a> by cattle can damage a forest seriously. Therefore, certain steps should be taken to prevent overgrazing by cattle.</li>
<li>Hunting and <a href="/wiki/Poaching" title="Poaching">poaching</a> should be banned.</li></ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zoological_parks">Zoological parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Zoological parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Zoological_park" class="mw-redirect" title="Zoological park">zoological parks</a> or zoos, live animals are kept for public <a href="/wiki/Recreation" title="Recreation">recreation</a>, education and conservation purposes. Modern zoos offer veterinary facilities, provide opportunities for threatened species to <a href="/wiki/Captive_breeding" title="Captive breeding">breed in captivity</a> and usually build environments that simulate the native habitats of the animals in their care. Zoos play a major role in creating <a href="/wiki/Environmental_awareness" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental awareness">awareness</a> about the need to conserve nature.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Botanical_gardens">Botanical gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Botanical gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical gardens</a>, plants are grown and displayed primarily for scientific and educational purposes. They consist of a collection of living plants, grown outdoors or under glass in <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse" title="Greenhouse">greenhouses</a> and conservatories. In addition, a botanical garden may include a collection of dried plants or <a href="/wiki/Herbarium" title="Herbarium">herbarium</a> and such facilities as lecture rooms, laboratories, libraries, museums and experimental or research plantings.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Resource_allocation">Resource allocation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Resource allocation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Focusing on limited areas of higher potential biodiversity promises greater immediate return on investment than spreading resources evenly or focusing on areas of little diversity but greater interest in biodiversity.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A second strategy focuses on areas that retain most of their original diversity, which typically require little or no restoration. These are typically non-urbanized, non-agricultural areas. Tropical areas often fit both criteria, given their natively high diversity and relative lack of development.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_status">Legal status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Legal status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hopetoun_falls.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Hopetoun_falls.jpg/220px-Hopetoun_falls.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Hopetoun_falls.jpg/330px-Hopetoun_falls.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Hopetoun_falls.jpg/440px-Hopetoun_falls.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hopetoun_falls.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A great deal of work is occurring to preserve the natural characteristics of <a href="/wiki/Hopetoun_Falls" title="Hopetoun Falls">Hopetoun Falls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> while continuing to allow visitor access.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International">International</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: International">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>United Nations <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a> (1992) and <a href="/wiki/Cartagena_Protocol_on_Biosafety" title="Cartagena Protocol on Biosafety">Cartagena Protocol on Biosafety</a>;</li>
<li>Convention on International Trade in Endangered Species (<a href="/wiki/CITES" title="CITES">CITES</a>);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ramsar_Convention" title="Ramsar Convention">Ramsar Convention</a> (Wetlands);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bonn_Convention" class="mw-redirect" title="Bonn Convention">Bonn Convention</a> on Migratory Species;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Convention" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Convention">World Heritage Convention</a> (indirectly by protecting biodiversity habitats)</li>
<li>Regional Conventions such as the Apia Convention</li>
<li>Bilateral agreements such as the <a href="/wiki/Japan-Australia_Migratory_Bird_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Japan-Australia Migratory Bird Agreement">Japan-Australia Migratory Bird Agreement</a>.</li></ul>
<p>Global agreements such as the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a>, give "sovereign national rights over biological resources" (not property). The agreements commit countries to "conserve biodiversity", "develop resources for sustainability" and "share the benefits" resulting from their use. Biodiverse countries that allow <a href="/wiki/Bioprospecting" title="Bioprospecting">bioprospecting</a> or collection of natural products, expect a share of the benefits rather than allowing the individual or institution that discovers/exploits the resource to capture them privately. Bioprospecting can become a type of <a href="/wiki/Biopiracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Biopiracy">biopiracy</a> when such principles are not respected.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Sovereignty principles can rely upon what is better known as <a href="/wiki/International_Treaty_on_Plant_Genetic_Resources_for_Food_and_Agriculture" title="International Treaty on Plant Genetic Resources for Food and Agriculture">Access and Benefit Sharing Agreements</a> (ABAs). The Convention on Biodiversity implies <a href="/wiki/Informed_consent" title="Informed consent">informed consent</a> between the source country and the collector, to establish which resource will be used and for what and to settle on a <a href="/wiki/International_Treaty_on_Plant_Genetic_Resources_for_Food_and_Agriculture" title="International Treaty on Plant Genetic Resources for Food and Agriculture">fair agreement on benefit sharing</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_level_laws">National level laws</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: National level laws">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Biodiversity is taken into account in some political and judicial decisions:
</p>
<ul><li>The relationship between law and ecosystems is very ancient and has consequences for biodiversity. It is related to private and public property rights. It can define protection for threatened ecosystems, but also some rights and duties (for example, <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a> and hunting rights).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li>Law regarding species is more recent. It defines species that must be protected because they may be threatened by extinction. The U.S. <a href="/wiki/Endangered_Species_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Endangered Species Act">Endangered Species Act</a> is an example of an attempt to address the "law and species" issue.</li>
<li>Laws regarding gene pools are only about a century old.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Domestication and plant breeding methods are not new, but advances in genetic engineering have led to tighter laws covering distribution of <a href="/wiki/Genetically_modified_organisms" class="mw-redirect" title="Genetically modified organisms">genetically modified organisms</a>, gene <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patents</a> and process patents.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> Governments struggle to decide whether to focus on for example, genes, genomes, or organisms and species.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li></ul>
<p>Uniform approval for use of biodiversity as a legal standard has not been achieved, however. Bosselman argues that biodiversity should not be used as a legal standard, claiming that the remaining areas of scientific uncertainty cause unacceptable administrative waste and increase litigation without promoting preservation goals.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>India passed the <a href="/wiki/Biological_Diversity_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Biological Diversity Act">Biological Diversity Act</a> in 2002 for the conservation of biological diversity in India. The Act also provides mechanisms for equitable sharing of benefits from the use of traditional biological resources and knowledge.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Analytical_limits">Analytical limits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Analytical limits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxonomic_and_size_relationships">Taxonomic and size relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Taxonomic and size relationships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Less than 1% of all species that have been described have been studied beyond simply noting their existence.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> The vast majority of Earth's species are microbial. Contemporary biodiversity physics is "firmly fixated on the visible [macroscopic] world".<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> For example, microbial life is <a href="/wiki/Metabolically" class="mw-redirect" title="Metabolically">metabolically</a> and environmentally more diverse than multicellular life (see e.g., <a href="/wiki/Extremophile" title="Extremophile">extremophile</a>). "On the tree of life, based on analyses of small-subunit <a href="/wiki/Ribosomal_RNA" title="Ribosomal RNA">ribosomal RNA</a>, visible life consists of barely noticeable twigs. The inverse relationship of size and population recurs higher on the evolutionary ladder—to a first approximation, all multicellular species on Earth are insects".<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Decline_in_insect_populations" title="Decline in insect populations">Insect extinction</a> rates are high—supporting the Holocene extinction hypothesis.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Diversity_study_.28botany.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Diversity_study_(botany)">Diversity study (botany)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Diversity study (botany)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The number of morphological attributes that can be scored for diversity study is generally limited and prone to environmental influences; thereby reducing the fine resolution required to ascertain the phylogenetic relationships. DNA based markers- microsatellites otherwise known as <i>simple sequence repeats</i> (SSR) were therefore used for the diversity studies of certain species and their wild relatives.
</p><p>In the case of <a href="/wiki/Cowpea" title="Cowpea">cowpea</a>, a study conducted to assess the level of genetic diversity in cowpea germplasm and related wide species, where the relatedness among various taxa were compared, primers useful for classification of taxa identified, and the origin and phylogeny of cultivated cowpea classified show that SSR markers are useful in validating with species classification and revealing the center of diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tools">Tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Tools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.globio.info/">GLOBIO</a>, an ongoing programme to map the past, current and future impacts of human activities on biodiversity</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20050825002841/http://stort.unep-wcmc.org/imaps/gb2002/book/viewer.htm">World Map of Biodiversity</a> an interactive map from the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Conservation_Monitoring_Centre" title="World Conservation Monitoring Centre">World Conservation Monitoring Centre</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://bison.usgs.gov/#home">Biodiversity Information Serving Our Nation (BISON)</a>, provides a United States gateway for serving, searching, mapping and downloading integrated species occurrence records from multiple data sources</li></ul>
